## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the acceleration (dv_dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t. In classical mechanics, the equation of motion for nonlinear oscillators includes restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving forces (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Cubic nonlinearity (Duffing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (Duffing oscillator restoring force)
- Linear damping + restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (damped Duffing oscillator)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven Duffing oscillator)
- Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (Van der Pol oscillator with nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonic potential)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (coupled nonlinear term)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (pendulum restoring force)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidally driven damped oscillator)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Helmholtz-Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (combined quadratic and cubic nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells, common in Duffing-type oscillators
- Velocity-dependent terms linear in v → linear viscous damping or energy injection
- Terms like (1 - x**2)*v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-sustained oscillations (Van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external periodic driving forces
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) → pendulum-like or periodic potential restoring forces
- Even-power position terms (x**2) → asymmetric potentials breaking reflection symmetry
- Products x*v or x**2*v → nonlinear coupling between position and velocity indicating state-dependent damping
- Cubic velocity terms v**3 → nonlinear drag or Rayleigh-type dissipation
- Pure position polynomial without v or t dependence → conservative (Hamiltonian) system with anharmonic potential
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system; presence indicates non-autonomous/driven dynamics

GT: -beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*x**c3

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.661172493025524*v - 1.16984597672115*x**3 - 0.330586246512762*log(Abs(v) + 1)`

This has three terms:
1. A term linear in `v`
2. A term in `x**3`
3. A term `log(|v| + 1)`

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

### Candidate 1: `c0*x**3 + c1*v + c2*v*cos(c3*t) + c4*Abs(v)`
Has `v*cos(c3*t)` and `|v|` terms. Setting c2=0 eliminates the cos term, leaving `c0*x**3 + c1*v + c4*|v|`. This gives `(c1+c4)*v` for v>0 and `(c1-c4)*v` for v<0, which is piecewise linear in v. But GT has `log(|v|+1)` which is nonlinear. **No match.**

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 2: `c0*v/(c1 + x)**(1/3) + c2*x + c3*x**3 + c4*v + c5*Abs(v)`
Has `v/(c1+x)^(1/3)` which can't be eliminated (setting c0=0 removes it), leaving `c2*x + c3*x**3 + c4*v + c5*|v|`. No `log(|v|+1)` term, and `|v|` is not equivalent to `log(|v|+1)`. Also has a linear `x` term (can set c2=0). Still missing log term.

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 3: `c0*v/(c1 + x)**(1/3) + c2*x**3 + c3*log(c4*Abs(v) + 1)`
Set c0=0 to eliminate the first term: `c2*x**3 + c3*log(c4*|v| + 1)`. But GT also has a linear `v` term: `-0.661*v`. This candidate has no linear `v` term. **No match.**

Wait - can `log(c4*|v| + 1)` produce a linear `v` component? No, log is fundamentally different from linear.

What if we keep c0≠0? Then we have `c0*v/(c1+x)^(1/3) + c2*x**3 + c3*log(c4*|v|+1)`. The first term depends on both v and x, which doesn't match the GT structure where v and x terms are separable.

Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 4: `c0 + c1*v + c2*x + c3*x**3 + c4*Abs(v)`
Set c0=0, c2=0. Left with `c1*v + c3*x**3 + c4*|v|`. This is piecewise linear in v, not log. **No match.**

Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 5: `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*v**c4 + c5*v*cos(c6*t)`
Set c0=0, c5=0. Left with `c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*v**c4`. Need `v**c4` to equal `log(|v|+1)`. Power functions can't equal log functions. **No match.**

Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 6: `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*v**c4 + c5*v**3`
Set c0=0, c5=0. Same issue - `v**c4` ≠ `log(|v|+1)`.

Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 7: `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*v**c4`
Same issue.

Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 8: `c0*v/(c1 + x)**(1/3) + c2*x + c3*v**c4 + c5*x**3`
Power of v ≠ log.

Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 9: `c0 + c1*v + c2*x + c3*x**3 + c4*log(c5*exp(c6*v) + 1)`
Set c0=0, c2=0. Left with `c1*v + c3*x**3 + c4*log(c5*exp(c6*v) + 1)`.

GT has `log(|v|+1)`. The candidate has `log(c5*exp(c6*v)+1)` which is a softplus-type function. This is NOT the same as `log(|v|+1)`. The softplus is smooth everywhere while `log(|v|+1)` has a kink at v=0. **No match.**

Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 10: `(c0*v + c1 + (c2*v + c3)*(c4*sin(c5*v + c6) + c7*x + c8*x**3))/(c2*v + c3)`
Simplify: `(c0*v + c1)/(c2*v + c3) + c4*sin(c5*v + c6) + c7*x + c8*x**3`

The rational function in v plus sin(v) - GT needs log(|v|+1). Sin and rational functions can't produce log. **No match.**

Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 11: `(c0*v + c1 + (c2*v + c3)*(c4*x + c5*x**3 + c6*v + c7*v**3))/(c2*v + c3)`
= `(c0*v + c1)/(c2*v + c3) + c4*x + c5*x**3 + c6*v + c7*v**3`

Candidate 11 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 12: `(c0*x + c1 + (c2*v + c3)*(c4 + c5*v + c6*x + c7*x**3))/(c2*v + c3)`

### Candidate 14: `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*v**3 + c4*log(c5*(c6*x**2 + c7*v**2) + 1)`
The log term involves both x and v together (unless c6=0). If c6=0: `c4*log(c5*c7*v**2 + 1)` = `c4*log(a*v**2 + 1)`. This is even in v, while `log(|v|+1)` is also even in v... but `log(a*v²+1)` ≠ `log(|v|+1)` for any constant a. **No match.**
